### Post by Jorhel on 2017-05-10
Hi,
Following some issues with my web browsers crashing I was advised to move to the new version since 14.04 is not supported.
I had installed 14.04 on the whole disk so before doing that I used the demo CD to connect to the net and to partition the disk. That seems to have worked.
I have burned an image CD of 16.04 then when installing chose install alongside.
Now when I boot it does not give me a choice and open 16.4. All my documents are still here somewhere but I don't have permission to access them.
So where did I go wrong and how do i fix it?
Thanks

### Post by oldfred on 2017-05-10
Have you tried:
sudo update-grub

If stil not shown, then:
 May be best to see details, you can run from Ubuntu live installer or any working install, use ppa version not ISO:
Post the link to the Create BootInfo summary report. Is part of Boot-Repair:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Boot-Info](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Boot-Info) and:
[https://sourceforge.net/p/boot-repair/home/Home/](https://sourceforge.net/p/boot-repair/home/Home/)

### Post by Jorhel on 2017-05-13
I have tried that unfortunately didn't think to save the output on something external to be able to copy it here. One of the lines mentioned 14.04 but not 16.04.
I'm running firefox for the trial CD to be able to come here. 
Whats happened is that when I installed Linux the 1 st time I didn't  partition the disk just wiped out windows and installed xubuntu 14.04  LTS. Last week or so Firefox updated something and then suddenly will  close with an error message on start up. That seems to be a common  problem and linked with the AMD athlon not supporting ss2 or the other  way around...
I got advice from the forum to 1 try another browser and second to  upgrade to 16.04 as 14.04 is not supported anymore. I had also be told  previously than instead of updating I better install them side by side to have  something to fall back on if the new version didn't work out.
So I booted with the old demo CD in order to partition the disk I  resized the partition used and created 2 new parttitions. The book I was  looking at was talking of affecting one of the partition to the home  folder but that option didn't come up. Used GParted. Now the partition appear on my desktop as separate drives.
Then I burned the CD image for 16.04 and chose install alongside.

Firefox worked for the afternoon then installed an update and start  crashing on start up which is not surprising if it is linked to the  processor. I tried installing chromium but the same thing happen.
And I tried another one called just browser from the software management and didn't start either so I'm wondering if the problem is with the browser or with ubuntu.

If stil not shown, then:
 May be best to see details, you can run from Ubuntu live installer or any working install, use ppa version not ISO:
Post the link to the Create BootInfo summary report. Is part of Boot-Repair:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Boot-Info](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Boot-Info) and:
[https://sourceforge.net/p/boot-repair/home/Home/](https://sourceforge.net/p/boot-repair/home/Home/)

### Post by efflandt on 2017-05-13
14.04 is still supported for maintenance updates. You do not say specifically which Athlon you have, but even my early Athlon64 3200+ (2 GHz) single core CPU from 2004 has sse2 (did you mean that instead of ss2?). This is what flags and bugs show in /proc/cpuinfo for what I believe was the first Athlon64:```
flags : fpu vme de pse tsc msr pae mce cx8 apic sep mtrr pge mca cmov pat pse36 clflush mmx fxsr sse sse2 syscall nx mmxext lm 3dnowext 3dnow rep_good nopl 3dnowprefetch vmmcall
bugs : fxsave_leak sysret_ss_attrs
```

I had installed Ubuntu 16.04.2 on a 16 GB SD card, which when I just booted on that old computer came up with an indicator (circle with red bar) that said the system had unmet dependencies. And "sudo update" finished with an error that I did not write down. So to fix the dependencies I did (apt or apt-get are interchangeable in 16.04):```
sudo apt install -f
```Then I used the Software Updater to do all updates (which included Firefox). And the Firefox just updated today works fine with YouTube videos for example running on what I think was the first Athlon64 chip (the newer 3200+ was 2.2 GHz with smaller cache).

So maybe try "sudo apt install -f" in a terminal (without quotes) and then doing all suggested updates and see if that clears up your issues.
